Kubernetes admission webhook processing chain is structured as a sophisticated system with multiple layers. The entry point is the generic Webhook dispatcher (in pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/) which implements the core Dispatcher interface. This generic webhook acts as an abstract base that handles common functionality like namespace/object selector matching, rule evaluation, and match conditions validation.\\n\\nThe processing chain splits into two specialized paths: (1) Mutating webhooks via MutatingAdmissionWebhook plugin and (2) Validating webhooks via ValidatingAdmissionWebhook plugin. Both plugins extend the generic Webhook class and use specialized dispatchers.\\n\\nThe mutating webhook dispatcher (mutating/dispatcher.go) implements sequential processing with reinvocation logic. It maintains a webhookReinvokeContext (in mutating/reinvocationcontext.go) to track which webhooks have been invoked and whether they should be reinvoked if mutations occur. The dispatcher calls callAttrMutatingHook for each webhook, which applies JSON patches to the object and handles side-effects validation. If a mutation changes the object, it triggers reinvocation of previously-invoked webhooks that have the IfNeededReinvocationPolicy.\\n\\nThe validating webhook dispatcher (validating/dispatcher.go) uses parallel dispatch with goroutines and sync.WaitGroup. It pre-computes all relevant hooks and caches versioned attributes before spawning parallel webhook calls. Each webhook runs in its own goroutine with panic recovery and handles the Ignore failure policy by continuing instead of returning errors.\\n\\nBoth dispatchers use the WebhookAccessor abstraction layer (accessors.go) which provides a unified interface for accessing webhook properties regardless of type. The WebhookAccessor interface has two implementations: mutatingWebhookAccessor and validatingWebhookAccessor. These accessors lazy-load and cache REST clients, label selectors, and compiled match condition matchers.\\n\\nThe webhook configurations come from the configuration managers (mutating_webhook_manager.go and validating_webhook_manager.go) which implement the Source interface. These managers watch the MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration API resources respectively, using informers to keep a cached, synced list of webhooks. Kubernetes admission webhook processing chain is structured as a sophisticated system with multiple layers. The entry point is the generic Webhook dispatcher (in pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/) which implements the core Dispatcher interface. This generic webhook acts as an abstract base that handles common functionality like namespace/object selector matching, rule evaluation, and match conditions validation.\\n\\nThe processing chain splits into two specialized paths: (1) Mutating webhooks via MutatingAdmissionWebhook plugin and (2) Validating webhooks via ValidatingAdmissionWebhook plugin. Both plugins extend the generic Webhook class and use specialized dispatchers.\\n\\nThe mutating webhook dispatcher (mutating/dispatcher.go) implements sequential processing with reinvocation logic. It maintains a webhookReinvokeContext (in mutating/reinvocationcontext.go) to track which webhooks have been invoked and whether they should be reinvoked if mutations occur. The dispatcher calls callAttrMutatingHook for each webhook, which applies JSON patches to the object and handles side-effects validation. If a mutation changes the object, it triggers reinvocation of previously-invoked webhooks that have the IfNeededReinvocationPolicy.\\n\\nThe validating webhook dispatcher (validating/dispatcher.go) uses parallel dispatch with goroutines and sync.WaitGroup. It pre-computes all relevant hooks and caches versioned attributes before spawning parallel webhook calls. Each webhook runs in its own goroutine with panic recovery and handles the Ignore failure policy by continuing instead of returning errors.\\n\\nBoth dispatchers use the WebhookAccessor abstraction layer (accessors.go) which provides a unified interface for accessing webhook properties regardless of type. The WebhookAccessor interface has two implementations: mutatingWebhookAccessor and validatingWebhookAccessor. These accessors lazy-load and cache REST clients, label selectors, and compiled match condition matchers.\\n\\nThe webhook configurations come from the configuration managers (mutating_webhook_manager.go and validating_webhook_manager.go) which implement the Source interface. These managers watch the MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration API resources respectively, using informers to keep a cached, synced list of webhooks. They create WebhookAccessor instances for each webhook in their configurations.\\n\\nThe API type definitions (admissionregistration/v1/types.go in kubernetes/api) define MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration as Kubernetes resources. Each configuration contains a list of webhooks with properties like ClientConfig, Rules, NamespaceSelector, ObjectSelector, FailurePolicy, TimeoutSeconds, SideEffects, and MatchConditions. MutatingWebhook additionally supports ReinvocationPolicy to enable reinvocation of eligible webhooks.\\n\\nThe chain flows: Webhook.Dispatch() -> plugin.ShouldCallHook() (with predicate matching and rule evaluation) -> dispatcher.Dispatch() (mutating or validating) -> callHook()/callAttrMutatingHook() -> webhook REST client invocation -> error handling and audit annotation recording. For mutating webhooks, patch application and reinvocation logic determines whether to trigger another round of webhook invocation.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Kubernetes admission webhook processing chain is structured as a sophisticated system with multiple layers. The entry point is the generic Webhook dispatcher (in pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/) which implements the core Dispatcher interface. This generic webhook acts as an abstract base that handles common functionality like namespace/object selector matching, rule evaluation, and match conditions validation.\\n\\nThe processing chain splits into two specialized paths: (1) Mutating webhooks via MutatingAdmissionWebhook plugin and (2) Validating webhooks via ValidatingAdmissionWebhook plugin. Both plugins extend the generic Webhook class and use specialized dispatchers.\\n\\nThe mutating webhook dispatcher (mutating/dispatcher.go) implements sequential processing with reinvocation logic. It maintains a webhookReinvokeContext (in mutating/reinvocationcontext.go) to track which webhooks have been invoked and whether they should be reinvoked if mutations occur. The dispatcher calls callAttrMutatingHook for each webhook, which applies JSON patches to the object and handles side-effects validation. If a mutation changes the object, it triggers reinvocation of previously-invoked webhooks that have the IfNeededReinvocationPolicy.\\n\\nThe validating webhook dispatcher (validating/dispatcher.go) uses parallel dispatch with goroutines and sync.WaitGroup. It pre-computes all relevant hooks and caches versioned attributes before spawning parallel webhook calls. Each webhook runs in its own goroutine with panic recovery and handles the Ignore failure policy by continuing instead of returning errors.\\n\\nBoth dispatchers use the WebhookAccessor abstraction layer (accessors.go) which provides a unified interface for accessing webhook properties regardless of type. The WebhookAccessor interface has two implementations: mutatingWebhookAccessor and validatingWebhookAccessor. These accessors lazy-load and cache REST clients, label selectors, and compiled match condition matchers.\\n\\nThe webhook configurations come from the configuration managers (mutating_webhook_manager.go and validating_webhook_manager.go) which implement the Source interface. These managers watch the MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration API resources respectively, using informers to keep a cached, synced list of webhooks. They create WebhookAccessor instances for each webhook in their configurations.\\n\\nThe API type definitions (admissionregistration/v1/types.go in kubernetes/api) define MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration as Kubernetes resources. Each configuration contains a list of webhooks with properties like ClientConfig, Rules, NamespaceSelector, ObjectSelector, FailurePolicy, TimeoutSeconds, SideEffects, and MatchConditions. MutatingWebhook additionally supports ReinvocationPolicy to enable reinvocation of eligible webhooks.\\n\\nThe chain flows: Webhook.Dispatch() -> plugin.ShouldCallHook() (with predicate matching and rule evaluation) -> dispatcher.Dispatch() (mutating or validating) -> callHook()/callAttrMutatingHook() -> webhook REST client invocation -> error handling and audit annotation recording. For mutating webhooks, patch application and reinvocation logic determines whether to trigger another round of webhook invocation.\"\n}\n","numLines":189,"startLine":1,"totalLines":189}}}
